`TF_DATA_DIR` changes the location where Terraform keeps its per-working-directory data, such as the current backend configuration.

By default this data is written into a `.terraform` subdirectory of the current directory, but the path given in `TF_DATA_DIR` will be used instead if non-empty.

In most cases it should not be necessary to set this variable, but it may be useful to do so if e.g. the working directory is not writable.

The data directory is used to retain data that must persist from one command to the next, so it's important to have this variable set consistently throughout all of the Terraform workflow commands (starting with `terraform init`) or else Terraform may be unable to find providers, modules, and other artifacts.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_workspace)
TF\_WORKSPACE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For multi-environment deployment, in order to select a workspace, instead of doing `terraform workspace select your_workspace`, it is possible to use this environment variable. Using TF\_WORKSPACE allow and override workspace selection.

For example:

    export TF_WORKSPACE=your_workspace
    

Using this environment variable is recommended only for non-interactive usage, since in a local shell environment it can be easy to forget the variable is set and apply changes to the wrong state.

For more information regarding workspaces, check out the section on [Using Workspaces](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.8.x/state/workspaces)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_in_automation)
TF\_IN\_AUTOMATION
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IN_AUTOMATION` is set to any non-empty value, Terraform adjusts its output to avoid suggesting specific commands to run next. This can make the output more consistent and less confusing in workflows where users don't directly execute Terraform commands, like in CI systems or other wrapping applications.

This is a purely cosmetic change to Terraform's human-readable output, and the exact output differences can change between minor Terraform versions.

For more details, see [Running Terraform in Automation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/automation/automate-terraform?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_discovery_retry)
TF\_REGISTRY\_DISCOVERY\_RETRY
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Set `TF_REGISTRY_DISCOVERY_RETRY` to configure the max number of request retries the remote registry client will attempt for client connection errors or 500-range responses that are safe to retry.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_client_timeout)
TF\_REGISTRY\_CLIENT\_TIMEOUT
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The default client timeout for requests to the remote registry is 10s. `TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT` can be configured and increased during exceptional circumstances.

    export TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT=15
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_config_file)
TF\_CLI\_CONFIG\_FILE
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The location of the [Terraform CLI configuration file](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/config-file)
.

    export TF_CLI_CONFIG_FILE="$HOME/.terraformrc-custom"
    

Note that `TERRAFORM_CONFIG` is a deprecated alias for the `TF_CLI_CONFIG_FILE` variable. We recommend using `TF_CLI_CONFIG_FILE` instead of the deprecated `TERRAFORM_CONFIG` variable.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_plugin_cache_dir)
TF\_PLUGIN\_CACHE\_DIR
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `TF_PLUGIN_CACHE_DIR` environment variable is an alternative way to set [the `plugin_cache_dir` setting in the CLI configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/config-file#provider-plugin-cache)
.

You can also use `TF_PLUGIN_CACHE_MAY_BREAK_DEPENDENCY_LOCK_FILE` to activate [the transitional compatibility setting `plugin_cache_may_break_dependency_lock_file`](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/config-file#allowing-the-provider-plugin-cache-to-break-the-dependency-lock-file)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#tf_ignore)
TF\_IGNORE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IGNORE` is set to "trace", Terraform will output debug messages to display ignored files and folders. This is useful when debugging large repositories with `.terraformignore` files.

    export TF_IGNORE=trace
    

For more details on `.terraformignore`, please see [Excluding Files from Upload with .terraformignore](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.8.x/settings/backends/remote#excluding-files-from-upload-with-terraformignore)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/config/environment-variables#hcp-terraform-cli-integration)
HCP Terraform CLI Integration
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The CLI integration with HCP Terraform lets you use HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise on the command line. The integration requires including a `cloud` block in your Terraform configuration. You can define its arguments directly in your configuration file or supply them through environment variables, which can be useful for non-interactive workflows like Continuous Integration (CI).

Refer to [HCP Terraform Settings](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/cloud/settings#environment-variables)
 for a full list of `cloud` block environment variables.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.8.x/docs/cli/config/environment-variables.mdx)

---

# Environment Variables | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.7.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/config/environment-variables)
.

Environment Variables
=====================

Terraform refers to a number of environment variables to customize various aspects of its behavior. None of these environment variables are required when using Terraform, but they can be used to change some of Terraform's default behaviors in unusual situations, or to increase output verbosity for debugging.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_log)
TF\_LOG
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Enables detailed logs to appear on stderr which is useful for debugging. For example:

    export TF_LOG=trace
    

To disable, either unset it, or set it to `off`. For example:

    export TF_LOG=off
    

For more on debugging Terraform, check out the section on [Debugging](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.7.x/debugging)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_log_path)
TF\_LOG\_PATH
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This specifies where the log should persist its output to. Note that even when `TF_LOG_PATH` is set, `TF_LOG` must be set in order for any logging to be enabled. For example, to always write the log to the directory you're currently running terraform from:

    export TF_LOG_PATH=./terraform.log
    

For more on debugging Terraform, check out the section on [Debugging](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.7.x/debugging)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_input)
TF\_INPUT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If set to "false" or "0", causes terraform commands to behave as if the `-input=false` flag was specified. This is used when you want to disable prompts for variables that haven't had their values specified. For example:

    export TF_INPUT=0
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_var_name)
TF\_VAR\_name
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Environment variables can be used to set variables. The environment variables must be in the format `TF_VAR_name` and this will be checked last for a value. For example:

    export TF_VAR_region=us-west-1
    export TF_VAR_ami=ami-049d8641
    export TF_VAR_alist='[1,2,3]'
    export TF_VAR_amap='{ foo = "bar", baz = "qux" }'
    

For more on how to use `TF_VAR_name` in context, check out the section on [Variable Configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.7.x/values/variables)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_args-and-tf_cli_args_name)
TF\_CLI\_ARGS and TF\_CLI\_ARGS\_name
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#)

The value of `TF_CLI_ARGS` will specify additional arguments to the command-line. This allows easier automation in CI environments as well as modifying default behavior of Terraform on your own system.

These arguments are inserted directly _after_ the subcommand (such as `plan`) and _before_ any flags specified directly on the command-line. This behavior ensures that flags on the command-line take precedence over environment variables.

For example, the following command: `TF_CLI_ARGS="-input=false" terraform apply -force` is the equivalent to manually typing: `terraform apply -input=false -force`.

The flag `TF_CLI_ARGS` affects all Terraform commands. If you specify a named command in the form of `TF_CLI_ARGS_name` then it will only affect that command. As an example, to specify that only plans never refresh, you can set `TF_CLI_ARGS_plan="-refresh=false"`.

The value of the flag is parsed as if you typed it directly to the shell. Double and single quotes are allowed to capture strings and arguments will be separated by spaces otherwise.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_data_dir)
TF\_DATA\_DIR
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`TF_DATA_DIR` changes the location where Terraform keeps its per-working-directory data, such as the current backend configuration.

By default this data is written into a `.terraform` subdirectory of the current directory, but the path given in `TF_DATA_DIR` will be used instead if non-empty.

In most cases it should not be necessary to set this variable, but it may be useful to do so if e.g. the working directory is not writable.

The data directory is used to retain data that must persist from one command to the next, so it's important to have this variable set consistently throughout all of the Terraform workflow commands (starting with `terraform init`) or else Terraform may be unable to find providers, modules, and other artifacts.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_workspace)
TF\_WORKSPACE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For multi-environment deployment, in order to select a workspace, instead of doing `terraform workspace select your_workspace`, it is possible to use this environment variable. Using TF\_WORKSPACE allow and override workspace selection.

For example:

    export TF_WORKSPACE=your_workspace
    

Using this environment variable is recommended only for non-interactive usage, since in a local shell environment it can be easy to forget the variable is set and apply changes to the wrong state.

For more information regarding workspaces, check out the section on [Using Workspaces](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.7.x/state/workspaces)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_in_automation)
TF\_IN\_AUTOMATION
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IN_AUTOMATION` is set to any non-empty value, Terraform adjusts its output to avoid suggesting specific commands to run next. This can make the output more consistent and less confusing in workflows where users don't directly execute Terraform commands, like in CI systems or other wrapping applications.

This is a purely cosmetic change to Terraform's human-readable output, and the exact output differences can change between minor Terraform versions.

For more details, see [Running Terraform in Automation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/automation/automate-terraform?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_discovery_retry)
TF\_REGISTRY\_DISCOVERY\_RETRY
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Set `TF_REGISTRY_DISCOVERY_RETRY` to configure the max number of request retries the remote registry client will attempt for client connection errors or 500-range responses that are safe to retry.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_client_timeout)
TF\_REGISTRY\_CLIENT\_TIMEOUT
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The default client timeout for requests to the remote registry is 10s. `TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT` can be configured and increased during exceptional circumstances.

    export TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT=15
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_config_file)
TF\_CLI\_CONFIG\_FILE
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The location of the [Terraform CLI configuration file](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/config-file)
.

    export TF_CLI_CONFIG_FILE="$HOME/.terraformrc-custom"
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_plugin_cache_dir)
TF\_PLUGIN\_CACHE\_DIR
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `TF_PLUGIN_CACHE_DIR` environment variable is an alternative way to set [the `plugin_cache_dir` setting in the CLI configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/config-file#provider-plugin-cache)
.

You can also use `TF_PLUGIN_CACHE_MAY_BREAK_DEPENDENCY_LOCK_FILE` to activate [the transitional compatibility setting `plugin_cache_may_break_dependency_lock_file`](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/config-file#allowing-the-provider-plugin-cache-to-break-the-dependency-lock-file)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#tf_ignore)
TF\_IGNORE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IGNORE` is set to "trace", Terraform will output debug messages to display ignored files and folders. This is useful when debugging large repositories with `.terraformignore` files.

    export TF_IGNORE=trace
    

For more details on `.terraformignore`, please see [Excluding Files from Upload with .terraformignore](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.7.x/settings/backends/remote#excluding-files-from-upload-with-terraformignore)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/config/environment-variables#terraform-cloud-cli-integration)
Terraform Cloud CLI Integration
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The CLI integration with Terraform Cloud lets you use Terraform Cloud and Terraform Enterprise on the command line. The integration requires including a `cloud` block in your Terraform configuration. You can define its arguments directly in your configuration file or supply them through environment variables, which can be useful for non-interactive workflows like Continuous Integration (CI).

Refer to [Terraform Cloud Settings](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.7.x/cloud/settings#environment-variables)
 for a full list of `cloud` block environment variables.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.7.x/docs/cli/config/environment-variables.mdx)

# Environment Variables | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.6.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/config/environment-variables)

TF\_INPUT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If set to "false" or "0", causes terraform commands to behave as if the `-input=false` flag was specified. This is used when you want to disable prompts for variables that haven't had their values specified. For example:

    export TF_INPUT=0
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_var_name)
TF\_VAR\_name
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Environment variables can be used to set variables. The environment variables must be in the format `TF_VAR_name` and this will be checked last for a value. For example:

    export TF_VAR_region=us-west-1
    export TF_VAR_ami=ami-049d8641
    export TF_VAR_alist='[1,2,3]'
    export TF_VAR_amap='{ foo = "bar", baz = "qux" }'
    

For more on how to use `TF_VAR_name` in context, check out the section on [Variable Configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.6.x/values/variables)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_args-and-tf_cli_args_name)
TF\_CLI\_ARGS and TF\_CLI\_ARGS\_name
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#)

The value of `TF_CLI_ARGS` will specify additional arguments to the command-line. This allows easier automation in CI environments as well as modifying default behavior of Terraform on your own system.

These arguments are inserted directly _after_ the subcommand (such as `plan`) and _before_ any flags specified directly on the command-line. This behavior ensures that flags on the command-line take precedence over environment variables.

For example, the following command: `TF_CLI_ARGS="-input=false" terraform apply -force` is the equivalent to manually typing: `terraform apply -input=false -force`.

The flag `TF_CLI_ARGS` affects all Terraform commands. If you specify a named command in the form of `TF_CLI_ARGS_name` then it will only affect that command. As an example, to specify that only plans never refresh, you can set `TF_CLI_ARGS_plan="-refresh=false"`.

The value of the flag is parsed as if you typed it directly to the shell. Double and single quotes are allowed to capture strings and arguments will be separated by spaces otherwise.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_data_dir)
TF\_DATA\_DIR
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`TF_DATA_DIR` changes the location where Terraform keeps its per-working-directory data, such as the current backend configuration.

By default this data is written into a `.terraform` subdirectory of the current directory, but the path given in `TF_DATA_DIR` will be used instead if non-empty.

In most cases it should not be necessary to set this variable, but it may be useful to do so if e.g. the working directory is not writable.

The data directory is used to retain data that must persist from one command to the next, so it's important to have this variable set consistently throughout all of the Terraform workflow commands (starting with `terraform init`) or else Terraform may be unable to find providers, modules, and other artifacts.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_workspace)
TF\_WORKSPACE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For multi-environment deployment, in order to select a workspace, instead of doing `terraform workspace select your_workspace`, it is possible to use this environment variable. Using TF\_WORKSPACE allow and override workspace selection.

For example:

    export TF_WORKSPACE=your_workspace
    

Using this environment variable is recommended only for non-interactive usage, since in a local shell environment it can be easy to forget the variable is set and apply changes to the wrong state.

For more information regarding workspaces, check out the section on [Using Workspaces](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.6.x/state/workspaces)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_in_automation)
TF\_IN\_AUTOMATION
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IN_AUTOMATION` is set to any non-empty value, Terraform adjusts its output to avoid suggesting specific commands to run next. This can make the output more consistent and less confusing in workflows where users don't directly execute Terraform commands, like in CI systems or other wrapping applications.

This is a purely cosmetic change to Terraform's human-readable output, and the exact output differences can change between minor Terraform versions.

For more details, see [Running Terraform in Automation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/automation/automate-terraform?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_discovery_retry)
TF\_REGISTRY\_DISCOVERY\_RETRY
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Set `TF_REGISTRY_DISCOVERY_RETRY` to configure the max number of request retries the remote registry client will attempt for client connection errors or 500-range responses that are safe to retry.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_client_timeout)
TF\_REGISTRY\_CLIENT\_TIMEOUT
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The default client timeout for requests to the remote registry is 10s. `TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT` can be configured and increased during exceptional circumstances.

    export TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT=15
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_config_file)
TF\_CLI\_CONFIG\_FILE
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The location of the [Terraform CLI configuration file](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/config-file)
.

    export TF_CLI_CONFIG_FILE="$HOME/.terraformrc-custom"
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_plugin_cache_dir)
TF\_PLUGIN\_CACHE\_DIR
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `TF_PLUGIN_CACHE_DIR` environment variable is an alternative way to set [the `plugin_cache_dir` setting in the CLI configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/config-file#provider-plugin-cache)
.

You can also use `TF_PLUGIN_CACHE_MAY_BREAK_DEPENDENCY_LOCK_FILE` to activate [the transitional compatibility setting `plugin_cache_may_break_dependency_lock_file`](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/config-file#allowing-the-provider-plugin-cache-to-break-the-dependency-lock-file)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#tf_ignore)
TF\_IGNORE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IGNORE` is set to "trace", Terraform will output debug messages to display ignored files and folders. This is useful when debugging large repositories with `.terraformignore` files.

    export TF_IGNORE=trace
    

For more details on `.terraformignore`, please see [Excluding Files from Upload with .terraformignore](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.6.x/settings/backends/remote#excluding-files-from-upload-with-terraformignore)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/config/environment-variables#terraform-cloud-cli-integration)
Terraform Cloud CLI Integration
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The CLI integration with Terraform Cloud lets you use Terraform Cloud and Terraform Enterprise on the command line. The integration requires including a `cloud` block in your Terraform configuration. You can define its arguments directly in your configuration file or supply them through environment variables, which can be useful for non-interactive workflows like Continuous Integration (CI).

Refer to [Terraform Cloud Settings](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.6.x/cloud/settings#environment-variables)
 for a full list of `cloud` block environment variables.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.6.x/docs/cli/config/environment-variables.mdx)

---

# Environment Variables | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.5.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/config/environment-variables)
.

Environment Variables
=====================

Terraform refers to a number of environment variables to customize various aspects of its behavior. None of these environment variables are required when using Terraform, but they can be used to change some of Terraform's default behaviors in unusual situations, or to increase output verbosity for debugging.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_log)
TF\_LOG
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Enables detailed logs to appear on stderr which is useful for debugging. For example:

    export TF_LOG=trace
    

To disable, either unset it, or set it to `off`. For example:

    export TF_LOG=off
    

For more on debugging Terraform, check out the section on [Debugging](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.5.x/debugging)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_log_path)
TF\_LOG\_PATH
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This specifies where the log should persist its output to. Note that even when `TF_LOG_PATH` is set, `TF_LOG` must be set in order for any logging to be enabled. For example, to always write the log to the directory you're currently running terraform from:

    export TF_LOG_PATH=./terraform.log
    

For more on debugging Terraform, check out the section on [Debugging](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.5.x/debugging)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_input)
TF\_INPUT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If set to "false" or "0", causes terraform commands to behave as if the `-input=false` flag was specified. This is used when you want to disable prompts for variables that haven't had their values specified. For example:

    export TF_INPUT=0
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_var_name)
TF\_VAR\_name
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Environment variables can be used to set variables. The environment variables must be in the format `TF_VAR_name` and this will be checked last for a value. For example:

    export TF_VAR_region=us-west-1
    export TF_VAR_ami=ami-049d8641
    export TF_VAR_alist='[1,2,3]'
    export TF_VAR_amap='{ foo = "bar", baz = "qux" }'
    

For more on how to use `TF_VAR_name` in context, check out the section on [Variable Configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.5.x/values/variables)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_args-and-tf_cli_args_name)
TF\_CLI\_ARGS and TF\_CLI\_ARGS\_name
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#)

The value of `TF_CLI_ARGS` will specify additional arguments to the command-line. This allows easier automation in CI environments as well as modifying default behavior of Terraform on your own system.

These arguments are inserted directly _after_ the subcommand (such as `plan`) and _before_ any flags specified directly on the command-line. This behavior ensures that flags on the command-line take precedence over environment variables.

For example, the following command: `TF_CLI_ARGS="-input=false" terraform apply -force` is the equivalent to manually typing: `terraform apply -input=false -force`.

The flag `TF_CLI_ARGS` affects all Terraform commands. If you specify a named command in the form of `TF_CLI_ARGS_name` then it will only affect that command. As an example, to specify that only plans never refresh, you can set `TF_CLI_ARGS_plan="-refresh=false"`.

The value of the flag is parsed as if you typed it directly to the shell. Double and single quotes are allowed to capture strings and arguments will be separated by spaces otherwise.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_data_dir)

.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

.

.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#tf_ignore)

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IGNORE` is set to "trace", Terraform will output debug messages to display ignored files and folders. This is useful when debugging large repositories with `.terraformignore` files.

    export TF_IGNORE=trace

.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/environment-variables#terraform-cloud-cli-integration)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can define its arguments directly in your configuration file or supply them through environment variables, which can be useful for non-interactive workflows like Continuous Integration (CI).

 for a full list of `cloud` block environment variables.

Terraform refers to a number of environment variables to customize various aspects of its behavior. None of these environment variables are required when using Terraform, but they can be used to change some of Terraform's default behaviors in unusual situations, or to increase output verbosity for debugging.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_log)
TF\_LOG
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Enables detailed logs to appear on stderr which is useful for debugging. For example:

    export TF_LOG=trace
    

To disable, either unset it, or set it to `off`. For example:

    export TF_LOG=off
    

For more on debugging Terraform, check out the section on [Debugging](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.3.x/debugging)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_log_path)
TF\_LOG\_PATH
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This specifies where the log should persist its output to. Note that even when `TF_LOG_PATH` is set, `TF_LOG` must be set in order for any logging to be enabled. For example, to always write the log to the directory you're currently running terraform from:

    export TF_LOG_PATH=./terraform.log
    

For more on debugging Terraform, check out the section on [Debugging](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.3.x/debugging)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_input)
TF\_INPUT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If set to "false" or "0", causes terraform commands to behave as if the `-input=false` flag was specified. This is used when you want to disable prompts for variables that haven't had their values specified. For example:

    export TF_INPUT=0
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_var_name)
TF\_VAR\_name
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Environment variables can be used to set variables. The environment variables must be in the format `TF_VAR_name` and this will be checked last for a value. For example:

    export TF_VAR_region=us-west-1
    export TF_VAR_ami=ami-049d8641
    export TF_VAR_alist='[1,2,3]'
    export TF_VAR_amap='{ foo = "bar", baz = "qux" }'
    

For more on how to use `TF_VAR_name` in context, check out the section on [Variable Configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.3.x/values/variables)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_args-and-tf_cli_args_name)
TF\_CLI\_ARGS and TF\_CLI\_ARGS\_name
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#)

The value of `TF_CLI_ARGS` will specify additional arguments to the command-line. This allows easier automation in CI environments as well as modifying default behavior of Terraform on your own system.

These arguments are inserted directly _after_ the subcommand (such as `plan`) and _before_ any flags specified directly on the command-line. This behavior ensures that flags on the command-line take precedence over environment variables.

For example, the following command: `TF_CLI_ARGS="-input=false" terraform apply -force` is the equivalent to manually typing: `terraform apply -input=false -force`.

The flag `TF_CLI_ARGS` affects all Terraform commands. If you specify a named command in the form of `TF_CLI_ARGS_name` then it will only affect that command. As an example, to specify that only plans never refresh, you can set `TF_CLI_ARGS_plan="-refresh=false"`.

The value of the flag is parsed as if you typed it directly to the shell. Double and single quotes are allowed to capture strings and arguments will be separated by spaces otherwise.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_data_dir)
TF\_DATA\_DIR
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`TF_DATA_DIR` changes the location where Terraform keeps its per-working-directory data, such as the current backend configuration.

By default this data is written into a `.terraform` subdirectory of the current directory, but the path given in `TF_DATA_DIR` will be used instead if non-empty.

In most cases it should not be necessary to set this variable, but it may be useful to do so if e.g. the working directory is not writable.

The data directory is used to retain data that must persist from one command to the next, so it's important to have this variable set consistently throughout all of the Terraform workflow commands (starting with `terraform init`) or else Terraform may be unable to find providers, modules, and other artifacts.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_workspace)
TF\_WORKSPACE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For multi-environment deployment, in order to select a workspace, instead of doing `terraform workspace select your_workspace`, it is possible to use this environment variable. Using TF\_WORKSPACE allow and override workspace selection.

For example:

    export TF_WORKSPACE=your_workspace
    

Using this environment variable is recommended only for non-interactive usage, since in a local shell environment it can be easy to forget the variable is set and apply changes to the wrong state.

For more information regarding workspaces, check out the section on [Using Workspaces](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.3.x/state/workspaces)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_in_automation)
TF\_IN\_AUTOMATION
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IN_AUTOMATION` is set to any non-empty value, Terraform adjusts its output to avoid suggesting specific commands to run next. This can make the output more consistent and less confusing in workflows where users don't directly execute Terraform commands, like in CI systems or other wrapping applications.

This is a purely cosmetic change to Terraform's human-readable output, and the exact output differences can change between minor Terraform versions.

For more details, see [Running Terraform in Automation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/automation/automate-terraform?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_discovery_retry)
TF\_REGISTRY\_DISCOVERY\_RETRY
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Set `TF_REGISTRY_DISCOVERY_RETRY` to configure the max number of request retries the remote registry client will attempt for client connection errors or 500-range responses that are safe to retry.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_registry_client_timeout)
TF\_REGISTRY\_CLIENT\_TIMEOUT
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The default client timeout for requests to the remote registry is 10s. `TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT` can be configured and increased during extraneous circumstances.

    export TF_REGISTRY_CLIENT_TIMEOUT=15
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_cli_config_file)
TF\_CLI\_CONFIG\_FILE
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The location of the [Terraform CLI configuration file](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/config-file)
.

    export TF_CLI_CONFIG_FILE="$HOME/.terraformrc-custom"
    

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#tf_ignore)
TF\_IGNORE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If `TF_IGNORE` is set to "trace", Terraform will output debug messages to display ignored files and folders. This is useful when debugging large repositories with `.terraformignore` files.

    export TF_IGNORE=trace
    

For more details on `.terraformignore`, please see [Excluding Files from Upload with .terraformignore](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1.3.x/settings/backends/remote#excluding-files-from-upload-with-terraformignore)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/config/environment-variables#terraform-cloud-cli-integration)
Terraform Cloud CLI Integration
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The CLI integration with Terraform Cloud lets you use Terraform Cloud and Terraform Enterprise on the command line. The integration requires including a `cloud` block in your Terraform configuration. You can define its arguments directly in your configuration file or supply them through environment variables, which can be useful for non-interactive workflows like Continuous Integration (CI).

Refer to [Terraform Cloud Settings](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.3.x/cloud/settings#environment-variables)
 for a full list of `cloud` block environment variables.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.3.x/docs/cli/config/environment-variables.mdx)

---

=====================

# terraform login command reference | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for pre-release version v1.13.x (beta). [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/login)
.

terraform login command
=======================

The `terraform login` command obtains an API token for HCP Terraform, Terraform Enterprise, or other host that offers Terraform services.

You can only use this command in interactive scenarios because the command launches a web browser on the same host where Terraform is running. If you are running Terraform in an unattended automation scenario, you can [configure credentials manually in the CLI configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x%20(beta)/config/config-file#credentials)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/commands/login#usage)
Usage
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform login [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log in to HCP Terraform at `app.terraform.io`.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/commands/login#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will obtain an API token and save it in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. When you run `terraform login`, it will explain specifically where it intends to save the API token and give you a chance to cancel if the current configuration is not as desired.

If you do not wish to store your API token in the default location, you can optionally configure a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x%20(beta)/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
 that knows how to store and later retrieve credentials in some other system, such as your organization's existing secrets management system.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/commands/login#login-server-support)
Login Server Support
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `terraform login` command works with any server supporting the [login protocol](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.13.x%20(beta)/login-protocol)
, including HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.13.x/docs/cli/commands/login.mdx)

---

# Get an API token for HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

Get an API token for HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise
===========================================================

This topic describes how to use the `terraform login` and `terraform logout` to authenticate with HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise.

> **Hands-on:** Try the [Authenticate the CLI with HCP Terraform](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/cloud/cloud-login?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
>  tutorial.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/auth#overview)
Overview
------------------------------------------------------------------------

[HCP Terraform](https://cloud.hashicorp.com/products/terraform)
 and [Terraform Enterprise](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/enterprise)
 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together.

You can integrate the Terraform CLI with HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise in the following ways:

*   Use the Terraform CLI as a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli)
     in HCP Terraform
*   Use HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise as a state backend and a private module registry.

These integrations require you to authenticate the Terraform CLI with your HCP Terraform account.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/auth#authentication)
Authentication
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Run the `terraform login` command to generate an API token for your HCP Terraform user account. Refer to the [`terraform login` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/login)
 reference documentation for details.

Run the `terraform logout` command to end your HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise session. Refer to the [`terraform logout` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout)
 reference documentation for details.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.12.x/docs/cli/auth/index.mdx)

---

# Command: login | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.5.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/login)
.

Command: login
==============

The `terraform login` command can be used to automatically obtain and save an API token for Terraform Cloud, Terraform Enterprise, or any other host that offers Terraform services.

**Note:** This command is suitable only for use in interactive scenarios where it is possible to launch a web browser on the same host where Terraform is running. If you are running Terraform in an unattended automation scenario, you can [configure credentials manually in the CLI configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/config-file#credentials)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/login#usage)
Usage
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform login [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log in to Terraform Cloud at `app.terraform.io`.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/login#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will obtain an API token and save it in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. When you run `terraform login`, it will explain specifically where it intends to save the API token and give you a chance to cancel if the current configuration is not as desired.

If you don't wish to store your API token in the default location, you can optionally configure a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
 which knows how to store and later retrieve credentials in some other system, such as your organization's existing secrets management system.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/login#login-server-support)
Login Server Support
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `terraform login` command works with any server supporting the [login protocol](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.5.x/login-protocol)
, including Terraform Cloud and Terraform Enterprise.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.5.x/docs/cli/commands/login.mdx)

---

# terraform logout command reference | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

terraform logout command
========================

This topic provides reference information about the `terraform logout` command.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout#introduction)
Introduction
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the `terraform logout` command to remove credentials stored after running the `terraform login` command. These credentials are API tokens for HCP Terraform, Terraform Enterprise, or any other host that offers Terraform services.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout#usage)
Usage
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform logout [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log out of HCP Terraform at `app.terraform.io`.

**Note:** the API token is only removed from local storage, not destroyed on the remote server, so it will remain valid until manually revoked.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will remove the token stored in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. If you have configured a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
, Terraform will use the helper's `forget` command to remove it.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.12.x/docs/cli/commands/logout.mdx)

---

# Command: login | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.1.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/login)
.

Command: login
==============

The `terraform login` command can be used to automatically obtain and save an API token for Terraform Cloud, Terraform Enterprise, or any other host that offers Terraform services.

**Note:** This command is suitable only for use in interactive scenarios where it is possible to launch a web browser on the same host where Terraform is running. If you are running Terraform in an unattended automation scenario, you can [configure credentials manually in the CLI configuration](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.1.x/config/config-file#credentials)
.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.1.x/commands/login#usage)
Usage
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform login [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log in to Terraform Cloud at `app.terraform.io`.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.1.x/commands/login#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will obtain an API token and save it in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. When you run `terraform login`, it will explain specifically where it intends to save the API token and give you a chance to cancel if the current configuration is not as desired.

If you don't wish to store your API token in the default location, you can optionally configure a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.1.x/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
 which knows how to store and later retrieve credentials in some other system, such as your organization's existing secrets management system.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.1.x/commands/login#login-server-support)
Login Server Support
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `terraform login` command works with any server supporting the [login protocol](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/internals/v1.1.x/login-protocol)
, including Terraform Cloud and Terraform Enterprise.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.1.x/docs/cli/commands/login.mdx)

---

# Authentication - Terraform CLI | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.5.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/auth)
.

CLI Authentication
==================

> **Hands-on:** Try the [Authenticate the CLI with Terraform Cloud](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/cloud/cloud-login?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
>  tutorial.

[Terraform Cloud](https://cloud.hashicorp.com/products/terraform)
 and [Terraform Enterprise](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/enterprise)
 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together. (For expediency, the content below refers to both products as "Terraform Cloud.")

Terraform CLI integrates with Terraform Cloud in several ways — it can be a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli/v1.5.x)
 in Terraform Cloud, and can also use Terraform Cloud as a state backend and a private module registry. All of these integrations require you to authenticate Terraform CLI with your Terraform Cloud account.

The best way to handle CLI authentication is with the `login` and `logout` commands, which help automate the process of getting an API token for your Terraform Cloud user account.

For details, see:

*   [The `terraform login` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/login)
    
*   [The `terraform logout` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/logout)
    

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.5.x/docs/cli/auth/index.mdx)

---

 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together. (For expediency, the content below refers to both products as "Terraform Cloud.")

Terraform CLI integrates with Terraform Cloud in several ways — it can be a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli/v1.2.x)
 in Terraform Cloud, and can also use Terraform Cloud as a state backend and a private module registry. All of these integrations require you to authenticate Terraform CLI with your Terraform Cloud account.

The best way to handle CLI authentication is with the `login` and `logout` commands, which help automate the process of getting an API token for your Terraform Cloud user account.

For details, see:

*   [The `terraform login` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.2.x/commands/login)
    
*   [The `terraform logout` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.2.x/commands/logout)

# Command: logout | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.5.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout)
.

Command: logout
===============

The `terraform logout` command is used to remove credentials stored by `terraform login`. These credentials are API tokens for Terraform Cloud, Terraform Enterprise, or any other host that offers Terraform services.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/logout#usage)
Usage
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform logout [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log out of Terraform Cloud at `app.terraform.io`.

**Note:** the API token is only removed from local storage, not destroyed on the remote server, so it will remain valid until manually revoked.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/commands/logout#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will remove the token stored in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. If you have configured a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.5.x/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
, Terraform will use the helper's `forget` command to remove it.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.5.x/docs/cli/commands/logout.mdx)

---

# terraform logout command reference | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for pre-release version v1.13.x (beta). [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout)
.

terraform logout command
========================

This topic provides reference information about the `terraform logout` command.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/commands/logout#introduction)
Introduction
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the `terraform logout` command to remove credentials stored after running the `terraform login` command. These credentials are API tokens for HCP Terraform, Terraform Enterprise, or any other host that offers Terraform services.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/commands/logout#usage)
Usage
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform logout [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log out of HCP Terraform at `app.terraform.io`.

**Note:** the API token is only removed from local storage, not destroyed on the remote server, so it will remain valid until manually revoked.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/commands/logout#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will remove the token stored in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. If you have configured a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x%20(beta)/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
, Terraform will use the helper's `forget` command to remove it.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.13.x/docs/cli/commands/logout.mdx)

---

# Get an API token for HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.11.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/auth)
.

Get an API token for HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise
===========================================================

This topic describes how to use the `terraform login` and `terraform logout` to authenticate with HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise.

> **Hands-on:** Try the [Authenticate the CLI with HCP Terraform](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/cloud/cloud-login?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
>  tutorial.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.11.x/auth#overview)
Overview
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[HCP Terraform](https://cloud.hashicorp.com/products/terraform)
 and [Terraform Enterprise](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/enterprise)
 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together.

You can integrate the Terraform CLI with HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise in the following ways:

*   Use the Terraform CLI as a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli/v1.11.x)
     in HCP Terraform
*   Use HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise as a state backend and a private module registry.

These integrations require you to authenticate the Terraform CLI with your HCP Terraform account.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.11.x/auth#authentication)
Authentication
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Run the `terraform login` command to generate an API token for your HCP Terraform user account. Refer to the [`terraform login` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.11.x/commands/login)
 reference documentation for details.

Run the `terraform logout` command to end your HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise session. Refer to the [`terraform logout` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.11.x/commands/logout)
 reference documentation for details.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.11.x/docs/cli/auth/index.mdx)

---

# Authentication - Terraform CLI | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.8.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/auth)
.

CLI Authentication
==================

> **Hands-on:** Try the [Authenticate the CLI with HCP Terraform](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/cloud/cloud-login?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
>  tutorial.

[HCP Terraform](https://cloud.hashicorp.com/products/terraform)
 and [Terraform Enterprise](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/enterprise)
 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together. (For expediency, the content below refers to both products as "HCP Terraform.")

Terraform CLI integrates with HCP Terraform in several ways — it can be a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli/v1.8.x)
 in HCP Terraform, and can also use HCP Terraform as a state backend and a private module registry. All of these integrations require you to authenticate Terraform CLI with your HCP Terraform account.

The best way to handle CLI authentication is with the `login` and `logout` commands, which help automate the process of getting an API token for your HCP Terraform user account.

For details, see:

*   [The `terraform login` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/commands/login)
    
*   [The `terraform logout` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.8.x/commands/logout)
    

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.8.x/docs/cli/auth/index.mdx)

---

# Command: logout | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for version v1.9.x. [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/commands/logout)
.

Command: logout
===============

The `terraform logout` command is used to remove credentials stored by `terraform login`. These credentials are API tokens for HCP Terraform, Terraform Enterprise, or any other host that offers Terraform services.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.9.x/commands/logout#usage)
Usage
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usage: `terraform logout [hostname]`

If you don't provide an explicit hostname, Terraform will assume you want to log out of HCP Terraform at `app.terraform.io`.

**Note:** the API token is only removed from local storage, not destroyed on the remote server, so it will remain valid until manually revoked.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.9.x/commands/logout#credentials-storage)
Credentials Storage
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Terraform will remove the token stored in plain text in a local CLI configuration file called `credentials.tfrc.json`. If you have configured a [credentials helper program](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.9.x/config/config-file#credentials-helpers)
, Terraform will use the helper's `forget` command to remove it.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.9.x/docs/cli/commands/logout.mdx)

---

 and [Terraform Enterprise](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/enterprise)
 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together. (For expediency, the content below refers to both products as "Terraform Cloud.")

Terraform CLI integrates with Terraform Cloud in several ways — it can be a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli/v1.1.x)
 in Terraform Cloud, and can also use Terraform Cloud as a state backend and a private module registry. All of these integrations require you to authenticate Terraform CLI with your Terraform Cloud account.

# Get an API token for HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise | Terraform | HashiCorp Developer

[HashiConf More sessions have been added to the conference agenda. Buy your pass and plan your schedule. Register](https://www.hashicorp.com/en/conferences/hashiconf/register)

Dismiss alert

[Terraform Home](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform)

You are viewing documentation for pre-release version v1.13.x (beta). [View latest version](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/auth)
.

Get an API token for HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise
===========================================================

This topic describes how to use the `terraform login` and `terraform logout` to authenticate with HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise.

> **Hands-on:** Try the [Authenticate the CLI with HCP Terraform](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/tutorials/cloud/cloud-login?utm_source=WEBSITE&utm_medium=WEB_IO&utm_offer=ARTICLE_PAGE&utm_content=DOCS)
>  tutorial.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/auth#overview)
Overview
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[HCP Terraform](https://cloud.hashicorp.com/products/terraform)
 and [Terraform Enterprise](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/enterprise)
 are platforms that perform Terraform runs to provision infrastructure, offering a collaboration-focused environment that makes it easier for teams to use Terraform together.

You can integrate the Terraform CLI with HCP Terraform and Terraform Enterprise in the following ways:

*   Use the Terraform CLI as a front-end for [CLI-driven runs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cloud-docs/run/cli/v1.13.x%20(beta))
     in HCP Terraform
*   Use HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise as a state backend and a private module registry.

These integrations require you to authenticate the Terraform CLI with your HCP Terraform account.

[](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x/auth#authentication)
Authentication
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Run the `terraform login` command to generate an API token for your HCP Terraform user account. Refer to the [`terraform login` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x%20(beta)/commands/login)
 reference documentation for details.

Run the `terraform logout` command to end your HCP Terraform or Terraform Enterprise session. Refer to the [`terraform logout` command](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/cli/v1.13.x%20(beta)/commands/logout)
 reference documentation for details.

[Edit this page on GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/web-unified-docs/blob/main/content/terraform/v1.13.x/docs/cli/auth/index.mdx)

---
